< review>
Recently moved to this neighborhood and happened to walk by and thought "this place looks like the type of place that would have good Mexican food", and I was not disappointed. I tried a chicken, carne asada, and al pastor taco. They were all tasty but the al pastor taco was my favorite. You can probably find cheaper Mexican food in other parts of LA, but for the South Bay the prices are a steal. I am sure I will be back too often for my own good. Just be aware they do charge an extra $1 for cards so try to have cash on hand.< /review>

<Review>I was passing through on the 215 and needed to stop for gas.  The Mobil on Newport Road seemed like a good place to stop since it was fairly close off the exit. The fitness center leaves a lot to be desired, as they only have a few machines and no barbells at all. The dumbbell set only goes up to 50lbs. as well, and one of the 35lbs dumbbells is missing.

It's pet friendly, and they provide waste bags for dogs which is nice. Yes, it's pricey to live here, but you have to know that going into it. It's unfair to the complex to move in and then complain about the cost of everything when you knew beforehand that that was the case.

All in all, it's been a pleasurable experience with the green scenery, beautiful trees, and our lovely apartment with its vaulted ceilings. All of our friends and family love coming over, and we love hosting. I would recommend this complex to anyone.< /review>< Pics>

< Review>
Heed the warnings of the reviewers and listen to the reviews...RENT AT YOUR OWN RISK!

I'm giving this place 2 stars because it hasn't been all bad living here. It's convenient (close to shopping, restaurants, and the highway), quiet for the most part (unless you live downstairs then can hear your upstairs neighbors because of thin floors), and pet friendly (if you want the option for a pet). However, after living for 2 yrs there, it's not as nice as they make it out to be. First of all the rent is RIDICULOUSLY expensive for even here in southern CA. If you look at their website, they want $2000-$8,000 for their 980 sq ft. Who has that kind of money? Unless you can live with roommates, there's no way a family could afford that. And the apartments aren't that nice for the price. Second, if you live in the back buildings, the lawn isn't maintained. There are dead trees and leaves covering the ground. Irresponsible pet owners leave dog feces in which the lawn and garden people don't pick it up but either mow over it or leave it so someone might step in it. Not to mention the dead rats that they take their time collecting after you've called to have them removed. Maintenance sometimes takes forever to address the issues in your apartment so you have to call to get someone (which I'm told is because they're low staffed). Then there are the fees. You have to pay for parking ($15 for non-covered, $30 for covered) PER vehicle. Water is not covered so you're paying for that as well which is split among your building so essentially you are paying for someone else's usage. And the water bill just went up (the complex cites as over consumption of water usage). Also, beware of the "hidden fees" (yes there are hidden fees despite what you're told). When you move out, expect to be hit with a fee for that as well as paying for trash and sewer (which was supposedly included in your rent) as well as any dings, dents, or scratches they find in which they constitute as "damages". They also take your deposit (without your knowledge or permission instead of getting it back) to add to your final move out charges. And then there's the issue of move out notifications. You have to give a 60 day notice to vacate but if you vacate within the 60 days, you're responsible for paying the FULL 2 months (unless they find a renter sooner in which you would be prorated for the days you stayed), which is not stated in the contract. CA law says you only are responsible for 30 days, regardless of personal policies.

If you have financial problems, don't expect these people to help. They only care about their money. They want you to pay for everything and don't care what your financial situation is. They lost my rent check TWICE, tried to blame me for not paying, then expected me to pay double. Luckily good rental history forced them to work with me. You can also not expect the onsite leasing manager to help either.

So moral of the story, rent here only if you want to be taken advantage of. I'm glad I'm out of there now. I've found a much better place to live and with landlords who seem to care.

(And yes "George" I know you say there's no hidden fees and you can help but there is from my own experience and I've tried but you didn't.)<//Review>

My significant other and I have lived here for 3 years. In the time that we have lived here it has been rather pleasant. The complex certainly has its pros and cons but overall I would say living here is good. Pros: Landscaping is always up to par and very accommodating to our pups. Maintenance crew is friendly, fast, and efficient.(Mario is our favorite). Amenities are always well kept (pool, laundry room, park etc.).The front office manager Jennifer Fitzmond (not sure about spelling) is compassionate and very understanding. The location is amazing with restaurants and stores all within walking distance. Cons: Rent goes up at least $80 with each lease renewal, kind of ridiculous if you ask me. Especially if your a loyal resident who pays rent on time and follows complex rules. Parking is a bit ridiculous its very limited and if you don't have a pass you WILL get towed.(but i understand that their needs to be rules) Also if you have your guests park on del dios there is no way to get inside the gate unless you walk all the way around to 9th ave and punch in the key code. They are pretty strict on hanging stuff over your blacony/deck. I've actually seen an off property manager push towels and blankets onto the ground as she walked pass each apartment that had stuff hanging over. A bit rude if you ask me. I understand it is to keep the ascetic appealing but if you go to the pool for the day or if your sweeping your floor and hang up stuff outside for a few hours i don't see the harm of it. Overall i'd say what has kept us here for 3 years is the great accommodations for our pets, the cleanliness of the complex and the location. <Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
I first met Dr. Kametz at the Carlsbad Marathon Expo January 18, 2014. I had been training pretty hard, but no harder than any other time I had run a half marathon. But I felt different I was having a hard time walking after a run to the point that I actually had a limp. So for about 10-days before the race I hadn't run. I couldn't. I was heartbroken at the expo, but still determined I would get up that next morning and attempt the race.

That's where Dr. Kametz comes in. I was supposed to run with my brother and sister. And my brother an advocate of Chiropractic (knowing I was a bit skeptical) suggested I at least talk to a Chiropractor.  I met Leigh and the Dr Kametz. He advised me not to run and to come see him early that next week.

As a runner I did the hardest thing a runner can do: I watched my brother and sister run from the sidelines.

I limped into Dr. Kametz's office where a smiling Leigh assured me that he would have me running again. Almost as if she was promising it.

The doctor took full size x-rays of my spine not just of the area I was complaining about. He went over them in detail and set up a plan to get me running again.

March 30, 2014 I ran in the Carlsbad 5000. Just 3 short months Leigh and Dr. Kametz came through with their promise.

I am 50-years old and stronger than ever.

If I could shout it from the mountain tops I would. Dr. Kametz is kind, compassionate, and a genius. He doesn't really like it when I say genius because he is so humble but he is!< /Text>

These people are amazing, truly amazing.</Text>

<Text>As someone who has had a life-time fear of the Dentist, Dr. Shelton has been an absolute game changer.  Unfortunately, avoiding the dentist did no favors to my teeth, and after spending years ignoring any type of check-up, I ended up with quite a few problems.  The last straw came after a wincing pain ruined what otherwise would have been a delicious meal.

I did some research, and settled on Polished General Dentistry after reading other reviews.  I was glad I did.  Everyone at Dr. Shelton's office is fantastic.  From the moment you walk into the office, you are made to feel at home.  The staff took extra care to make sure my nerves were calm, and made sure to listen to my complaints about previous experiences.

Besides the staff being a pleasure to have look after you, Dr. Shelton herself clearly cares about her profession.  She uses cutting edge technologies to give the best possible diagnoses, and then delivers (in what my case was bad news) with care.  Her treatment plan was extremely effective, and I never felt in pain or worried about my next visit (as I almost always did in the past).

‚Ä¢	The science is in front of your face  Invisalign treatment depends solely on you.  Like everything else in life, if you want quality results, you must put in quality work.  Stick to the script.

I‚Äôve put together some info for you and others to understand the necessity and safety surrounding dental X-rays.\n\nIt‚Äôs important for us as your dental professional to have a comprehensive picture of all your teeth because gum disease and cavities don‚Äôt often cause pain in the beginning stages, which is why detecting them with X-rays is imperative. <Review>If you enjoyed this review please give it a like. Elena's crepes is a quaint artsy fun spot located at the entrance of Oceansides artist alley. This is a decadent treat, I had the ham and cheese crepe and my Mother in law enjoyed her egg salad crepe. The crepes are delicate and light and scrumptious, almost sinful.
Elana and her husband Hassan have been serving up scrumptious crepes in Oceanside for four years. Their artwork is proudly displayed on the walls.
